001package squidpony;
002
003import regexodus.*;
004import squidpony.squidmath.*;
005
006import java.io.Serializable;
007import java.util.*;
008
009/**
010 * A text generator for producing sentences and/or words in nonsense languages that fit a theme. This does not use an
011 * existing word list as a basis for its output, so it may or may not produce existing words occasionally, but you can
012 * safely assume it won't generate a meaningful sentence except in the absolute unlikeliest of cases.
013 * Created by Tommy Ettinger on 11/29/2015.
014 *
015 * @author Tommy Ettinger
016 */
017
018public class FakeLanguageGen implements Serializable {
019    private static final long serialVersionUID = -2396642435461186352L;
020    public final String[] openingVowels, midVowels, openingConsonants, midConsonants, closingConsonants,
021            vowelSplitters, closingSyllables;
022    public final boolean clean;
023    public final IntDoubleOrderedMap syllableFrequencies;
024    protected double totalSyllableFrequency = 0.0;
025    public final double vowelStartFrequency, vowelEndFrequency, vowelSplitFrequency, syllableEndFrequency;
026    public final Pattern[] sanityChecks;
027    public ArrayList<Modifier> modifiers;
028    public static final StatefulRNG srng = new StatefulRNG();
029    private static final OrderedSet<FakeLanguageGen> registry = new OrderedSet<>(32);
030    protected String summary = null;
031    /**
032     * A pattern String that will match any vowel FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including Latin, Greek,
033     * and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex ({@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
034     */
035    public static final String anyVowel = "[àáâãäåæāăąǻǽaèéêëēĕėęěeìíîïĩīĭįıiòóôõöøōŏőœǿoùúûüũūŭůűųuýÿŷỳyαοειυаеёийоуъыэюя]",
036    /**
037     * A pattern String that will match one or more of any vowels FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including
038     * Latin, Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex
039     * ({@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
040     */
041    anyVowelCluster = anyVowel + '+',
042    /**
043     * A pattern String that will match any consonant FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including Latin,
044     * Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex ({@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
045     */
046    anyConsonant = "[bcçćĉċčdþðďđfgĝğġģhĥħjĵȷkķlĺļľŀłmnñńņňŋpqrŕŗřsśŝşšștţťțvwŵẁẃẅxyýÿŷỳzźżžṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥρσζτκχνθμπψβλγφξςбвгдклпрстфхцжмнзчшщ]",
047    /**
048     * A pattern String that will match one or more of any consonants FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box,
049     * including Latin, Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex
050     * ({@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
051     */
052    anyConsonantCluster = anyConsonant + '+';
053    protected static final Pattern repeats = Pattern.compile("(.)\\1+"),
054            vowelClusters = Pattern.compile(anyVowelCluster, REFlags.IGNORE_CASE | REFlags.UNICODE),
055            consonantClusters = Pattern.compile(anyConsonantCluster, REFlags.IGNORE_CASE | REFlags.UNICODE);
056    //latin
057    //àáâãäåæāăąǻǽaèéêëēĕėęěeìíîïĩīĭįıiòóôõöøōŏőœǿoùúûüũūŭůűųuýÿŷỳybcçćĉċčdþðďđfgĝğġģhĥħjĵȷkķlĺļľŀłmnñńņňŋpqrŕŗřsśŝşšștţťțvwŵẁẃẅxyýÿŷỳzźżžṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥ
058    //ÀÁÂÃÄÅÆĀĂĄǺǼAÈÉÊËĒĔĖĘĚEÌÍÎÏĨĪĬĮIIÒÓÔÕÖØŌŎŐŒǾOÙÚÛÜŨŪŬŮŰŲUÝŸŶỲYBCÇĆĈĊČDÞÐĎĐFGĜĞĠĢHĤĦJĴȷKĶLĹĻĽĿŁMNÑŃŅŇŊPQRŔŖŘSŚŜŞŠȘTŢŤȚVWŴẀẂẄXYÝŸŶỲZŹŻŽṚṜḶḸḌṬṄṆṢṂḤ
059    //greek
060    //αοειυρσζτκχνθμπψβλγφξς
061    //ΑΟΕΙΥΡΣΖΤΚΧΝΘΜΠΨΒΛΓΦΞ
062    //cyrillic
063    //аеёийоуъыэюябвгдклпрстфхцжмнзчшщ
064    //АЕЁИЙОУЪЫЭЮЯБВГДКЛПРСТФХЦЖМНЗЧШЩ

066    static final Pattern[]
067            vulgarChecks = new Pattern[]
068            {
069                    //17 is REFlags.UNICODE | REFlags.IGNORE_CASE
070                    Pattern.compile("[sξζzkкκcсς][hнlι].{1,3}[dtтτΓг]", 17),
071                    Pattern.compile("(?:(?:[pрρ][hн])|[fd]).{1,3}[kкκcсςxхжχq]", 17), // lots of these end in a 'k' sound, huh
072                    Pattern.compile("[kкκcсςСQq][uμυνvhн]{1,3}[kкκcсςxхжχqmм]", 17),
073                    Pattern.compile("[bъыбвβЪЫБ].?[iτιyуλγУ].?[cсς]", 17),
074                    Pattern.compile("[hн][^aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУ][^aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУ]?[rяΓ]", 17),
075                    Pattern.compile("[tтτΓгcсς][iτιyуλγУ][tтτΓг]+$", 17),
076                    Pattern.compile("(?:(?:[pрρ][hн])|f)[aаαΛhн]{1,}[rяΓ][tтτΓг]", 17),
077                    Pattern.compile("[Ssξζzcсς][hн][iτιyуλγУ].?[sξζzcсς]", 17),
078                    Pattern.compile("[aаαΛ][nи][aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУoоюσοuμυνv]{1,2}[Ssξlιζz]", 17),
079                    Pattern.compile("[aаαΛ]([sξζz]{2})", 17),
080                    Pattern.compile("[kкκcсςСQq][hн]?[uμυνv]([hн]?)[nи]+[tтτΓг]", 17),
081                    Pattern.compile("[nиfvν]..?[jg]", 17), // might as well remove two possible slurs and a body part with one check
082                    Pattern.compile("[pрρ](?:(?:([eезξεЗΣoоюσοuμυνv])\\1)|(?:[eезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУuμυνv]+[sξζz]))", 17), // the grab bag of juvenile words
083                    Pattern.compile("[mм][hнwψшщ]?..?[rяΓ].?d", 17), // should pick up the #1 obscenity from Spanish and French
084                    Pattern.compile("[g][hн]?[aаαАΑΛeеёзξεЕЁЗΕΣ][yуλγУeеёзξεЕЁЗΕΣ]", 17), // could be inappropriate for random text
085                    Pattern.compile("[wψшщuμυνv](?:[hн]?)[aаαΛeеёзξεЗΕΣoоюσοuμυνv](?:[nи]+)[gkкκcсςxхжχq]", 17)
086            },
087            genericSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
088                    {
089                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
090                            Pattern.compile("(\\p{L})\\1\\1"),
091                            Pattern.compile("[Ii][iyqhl]"),
092                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]([aiu])\\1"),
093                            Pattern.compile("[Rr][aeiouy]+[rh]"),
094                            Pattern.compile("[Qq]u[yu]"),
095                            Pattern.compile("[^oaei]uch"),
096                            Pattern.compile("[Hh][tcszi]?h"),
097                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]t[^aeiouy]{2}"),
098                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]h([^aeiouy]|$)"),
099                            Pattern.compile("([xqy])\\1$"),
100                            Pattern.compile("[qi]y$"),
101                            Pattern.compile("[szSZrlRL]+?[^aeiouytdfgkcpbmnslrv][rlsz]"),
102                            Pattern.compile("[UIuiYy][wy]"),
103                            Pattern.compile("^[UIui][ae]"),
104                            Pattern.compile("^([^aeiouyl])\\1", 17)
105                    },
106            englishSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
107                    {
108                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
109                            Pattern.compile("(\\w)\\1\\1"),
110                            Pattern.compile("(.)\\1(.)\\2"),
111                            Pattern.compile("[Aa][ae]"),
112                            Pattern.compile("[Uu][umlkj]"),
113                            Pattern.compile("[Ii][iyqkhrl]"),
114                            Pattern.compile("[Oo][c]"),
115                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]([aiu])\\1"),
116                            Pattern.compile("[Rr][aeiouy]+[rh]"),
117                            Pattern.compile("[Qq]u[yu]"),
118                            Pattern.compile("[^oaei]uch"),
119                            Pattern.compile("[Hh][tcszi]?h"),
120                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]t[^aeiouy]{2}"),
121                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]h([^aeiouy]|$)"),
122                            Pattern.compile("[szSZrlRL]+?[^aeiouytdfgkcpbmnslr][rlsz]"),
123                            Pattern.compile("[UIuiYy][wy]"),
124                            Pattern.compile("^[UIui][ae]"),
125                            Pattern.compile("q(?:u?)$")
126                    },
127            japaneseSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
128                    {
129                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
130                            Pattern.compile("(\\w)\\1\\1"),
131                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]s[^u]"),
132                            Pattern.compile("[Ff][^u]"),
133                            Pattern.compile("[Yy][^auo]"),
134                            Pattern.compile("[Tt][ui]"),
135                            Pattern.compile("[SsZzDd]i"),
136                            Pattern.compile("[Hh]u"),
137                    },
138            arabicSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
139                    {
140                            Pattern.compile("(.)\\1\\1"),
141                            Pattern.compile("-[^aeiou](?:[^aeiou]|$)"),
142                    };

385    /*
386     * Removes accented characters from a string; if the "base" characters are non-English anyway then the result won't
387     * be an ASCII string, but otherwise it probably will be.
388     * <br>
389     * Credit to user hashable from http://stackoverflow.com/a/1215117
390     *
391     * @param str a string that may contain accented characters
392     * @return a string with all accented characters replaced with their (possibly ASCII) counterparts
393     *
394    public String removeAccents(String str) {
395        String alteredString = Normalizer.normalize(str, Normalizer.Form.NFD);
396        alteredString = diacritics.matcher(alteredString).replaceAll("");
397        alteredString = alteredString.replace('æ', 'a');
398        alteredString = alteredString.replace('œ', 'o');
399        alteredString = alteredString.replace('Æ', 'A');
400        alteredString = alteredString.replace('Œ', 'O');
401        return alteredString;
402    }*/
403
404    /**
405     * Removes accented Latin-script characters from a string; if the "base" characters are non-English anyway then the
406     * result won't be an ASCII string, but otherwise it probably will be.
407     *
408     * @param str a string that may contain accented Latin-script characters
409     * @return a string with all accented characters replaced with their (possibly ASCII) counterparts
410     */
411    public static CharSequence removeAccents(CharSequence str) {
412        CharSequence alteredString = str;
413        for (int i = 0; i < accentFinders.length; i++) {
414            alteredString = accentFinders[i].replace(alteredString);
415        }
416        return alteredString;
417    }
418
419    private FakeLanguageGen register() {
420        summary = registry.size() + "@1";
421        registry.add(this);
422        return copy();
423    }
424
425    private FakeLanguageGen summarize(String brief) {
426        summary = brief;
427        return this;
428    }

773    /**
774     * Swahili is one of the more commonly-spoken languages in sub-Saharan Africa, and serves mainly as a shared language
775     * that is often learned after becoming fluent in one of many other (vaguely-similar) languages of the area. An
776     * example sentence in Swahili, that this might try to imitate aesthetically, is "Mtoto mdogo amekisoma," meaning
777     * "The small child reads it" (where it is a book). A notable language feature used here is the redoubling of words,
778     * which is used in Swahili to emphasize or alter the meaning of the doubled word; here, it always repeats exactly
779     * and can't make minor changes like a real language might. This generates things like "gata-gata", "hapi-hapi", and
780     * "mimamzu-mimamzu", always separating with a hyphen here.
781     * <br>
782     * As an aside, please try to avoid the ugly stereotypes that fantasy media often assigns to speakers of African-like
783     * languages when using this or any of the generators. Many fantasy tropes come from older literature written with
784     * major cultural biases, and real-world cultural elements can be much more interesting to players than yet another
785     * depiction of a "jungle savage" with stereotypical traits. Consider drawing from existing lists of real-world
786     * technological discoveries, like https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Africa , for
787     * inspiration when world-building; though some groups may not have developed agriculture by early medieval times,
788     * their neighbors may be working iron and studying astronomy just a short distance away.
789     * <br>
790     * Kondueyu; ma mpiyamdabota mise-mise nizakwaja alamsa amja, homa nkajupomba.
791     */
792    public static final FakeLanguageGen SWAHILI = swahili().register();

837     * closest to the northern dialect), which due to the previously mentioned properties, makes it especially good for
838     * mixing with other languages to make letter combinations that seem strange to appear. It is unlikely that this
839     * particular generated language style will be familiar to readers, so it probably won't have existing stereotypes
840     * associated with the text. One early comment this received was, "it looks like a bunch of letters semi-randomly
841     * thrown together", which is probably a typical response (the comment was made by someone fluent in German and
842     * English, and most Western European languages are about as far as you can get from Somali).
843     * <br>
844     * Libor cat naqoxekh dhuugad gisiqir?
845     */

1203    /**
1204     * Imitation Hindi, romanized to use the Latin alphabet using accented glyphs similar to the IAST standard.
1205     * Most fonts do not support the glyphs that IAST-standard romanization of Hindi needs, so this uses alternate
1206     * glyphs from at most Latin Extended-A. Relative to the IAST standard, the glyphs {@code "ṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥ"} become
1207     * {@code "ŗŕļĺđţńņşĕĭ"}, with the nth glyph in the first string being substituted with the nth glyph in the second
1208     * string. You may want to get a variant on this language with {@link #removeAccents()} if you can't display the
1209     * less-commonly-supported glyphs {@code āīūĕĭáíúóŗŕļţĺđńñņśş}. For some time SquidLib had a separate version of
1210     * imitation Hindi that was accurate to the IAST standard, but this version is more usable because font support is
1211     * much better for the glyphs it uses, so the IAST kind was removed (it added quite a bit of code for something that
1212     * was mostly unusable).
1213     * <br>
1214     * Darvāga yar; ghađhinopŕauka āĕrdur, conśaigaijo śabhodhaĕđū jiviđaudu.
1215     */
1216    public static final FakeLanguageGen HINDI_ROMANIZED = hindi().register();
1217
1218    private static FakeLanguageGen arabic(){
1219        return new FakeLanguageGen(
1220                new String[]{"a", "a", "a", "a", "a", "a", "aa", "aa", "aa", "ai", "au",

1257    /**
1258     * Imitation Arabic, using mostly the Latin alphabet but with some Greek letters for tough transliteration topics.
1259     * It's hard to think of a more different (widely-spoken) language to romanize than Arabic. Written Arabic does not
1260     * ordinarily use vowels (the writing system is called an abjad, in contrast to an alphabet), and it has more than a
1261     * few sounds that are very different from those in English. This version, because of limited support in fonts and
1262     * the need for separate words to be distinguishable with regular expressions, uses somewhat-accurate digraphs or
1263     * trigraphs instead of the many accented glyphs (not necessarily supported by most fonts) in most romanizations of
1264     * Arabic, and this scheme uses no characters from outside ASCII.
1265     * <br>
1266     * Please try to be culturally-sensitive about how you use this generator. Classical Arabic (the variant that
1267     * normally marks vowels explicitly and is used to write the Qur'an) has deep religious significance in Islam, and
1268     * if you machine-generate text that (probably) isn't valid Arabic, but claim that it is real, or that it has
1269     * meaning when it actually doesn't, that would be an improper usage of what this generator is meant to do. In a
1270     * fantasy setting, you can easily confirm that the language is fictional and any overlap is coincidental; an
1271     * example of imitation Arabic in use is the Dungeons and Dragons setting, Al-Qadim, which according to one account
1272     * sounds similar to a word in real Arabic (that does not mean anything like what the designer was aiming for). In a
1273     * historical setting, FakeLanguageGen is probably "too fake" to make a viable imitation for any language, and may
1274     * just sound insulting if portrayed as realistic. You may want to mix ARABIC_ROMANIZED with a very different kind
1275     * of language, like GREEK_ROMANIZED or RUSSIAN_AUTHENTIC, to emphasize that this is not a real-world language.
1276     * <br>
1277     * Hiijakki al-aafusiib rihit, ibn-ullukh aj shwisari!
1278     */
1279    public static final FakeLanguageGen ARABIC_ROMANIZED = arabic().register();

1342     * properly called Yupik or Yup'ik, and primarily spoken in Siberia instead of Canada and Alaska).

1400    /**
1401     * Somewhat close to Old Norse, which is itself very close to Icelandic, so this uses Icelandic spelling rules. Not
1402     * to be confused with the language(s) of Norway, where the Norwegian languages are called norsk, and are further
1403     * distinguished into Bokmål and Nynorsk. This should not be likely to seem like any form of Norwegian, since it
1404     * doesn't have the a-with-ring letter 'å' and has the letters eth ('Ðð') and thorn (Þþ). If you want to remove any
1405     * letters not present on a US-ASCII keyboard, you can use {@link Modifier#SIMPLIFY_NORSE} on this language or some
1406     * mix of this with other languages; it also changes some of the usage of "j" where it means the English "y" sound,
1407     * making "fjord" into "fyord", which is closer to familiar uses from East Asia like "Tokyo" and "Pyongyang".
1408     * <br>
1409     * Leyrk tjör stomri kna snó æd ðrépdápá, prygso?
1410     */
1411    public static final FakeLanguageGen NORSE = norse().register();

1471    /**
1472     * A mix of four different languages, using only ASCII characters, that is meant for generating single words for
1473     * creature or place names in fantasy settings.
1474     * <br>
1475     * Adeni, Sainane, Caneros, Sune, Alade, Tidifi, Muni, Gito, Lixoi, Bovi...
1476     */
1477    public static final FakeLanguageGen FANTASY_NAME = GREEK_ROMANIZED.mix(
1478            RUSSIAN_ROMANIZED.mix(
1479                    FRENCH.removeAccents().mix(
1480                            JAPANESE_ROMANIZED, 0.5), 0.85), 0.925).register();
1481    /**
1482     * A mix of four different languages with some accented characters added onto an ASCII base, that can be good for
1483     * generating single words for creature or place names in fantasy settings that should have a "fancy" feeling from
1484     * having unnecessary accents added primarily for visual reasons.
1485     * <br>
1486     * Askieno, Blarcīnũn, Mēmida, Zizhounkô, Blęrinaf, Zemĭ, Mónazôr, Renerstă, Uskus, Toufounôr...
1487     */
1488    public static final FakeLanguageGen FANCY_FANTASY_NAME = FANTASY_NAME.addAccents(0.47, 0.07).register();

1642     * Fantasy language that might be suitable for a language spoken by demons, aggressive warriors, or people who seek
1643     * to emulate or worship similar groups. The tendency here is for DEMONIC to be the language used by creatures that
1644     * are considered evil because of their violence, while INFERNAL would be the language used by creatures that are
1645     * considered evil because of their manipulation and deceit (DEMONIC being "chaotic evil" and INFERNAL being "lawful
1646     * evil"). This uses lots of sounds that don't show up in natural languages very often, mixing harsh or guttural
1647     * sounds like "kh" and "ghr" with rare sounds like "vr", "zv", and "tl". It uses vowel-splitting in a way that is
1648     * similar to LOVECRAFT, sometimes producing sounds like "tsa'urz" or "khu'olk".
1649     * <br>
1650     * Vrirvoks xatughat ogz; olds xu'oz xorgogh!
1651     */

1680    /**
1681     * Fantasy language that might be suitable for a language spoken by fiends, users of witchcraft, or people who seek
1682     * to emulate or worship similar groups. The tendency here is for DEMONIC to be the language used by creatures that
1683     * are considered evil because of their violence, while INFERNAL is the language used by creatures that are
1684     * considered evil because of their manipulation and deceit (DEMONIC being "chaotic evil" and INFERNAL being "lawful
1685     * evil"). The name INFERNAL refers to Dante's Inferno and the various naming conventions used for residents of Hell
1686     * in the more-modern Christian traditions (as well as some of the stylistic conventions of Old Testament figures
1687     * described as false idols, such as Moloch and Mammon). In an effort to make this distinct from the general style
1688     * of names used in ancient Hebrew (since this is specifically meant for the names of villains as opposed to normal
1689     * humans), we add in vowel splits as used in LOVECRAFT and DEMONIC, then add quite a few accented vowels. These
1690     * traits make the language especially well-suited for "deal with the Devil" written bargains, where a single accent
1691     * placed incorrectly could change the meaning of a contract and provide a way for a fiend to gain leverage.
1692     * <br>
1693     * Zézîzûth eke'iez áhìphon; úhiah îbbëphéh haîtemheû esmez...
1694     */
1695    public static final FakeLanguageGen INFERNAL = infernal().register();

1858    /**
1859     * Imitation text from an approximation of Korean, using the Revised Romanization method that is official in South
1860     * Korea today and is easier to type. The text this makes may be hard to pronounce. Korean is interesting as a
1861     * language to imitate for a number of reasons; many of the sounds in it are rarely found elsewhere, it can cluster
1862     * consonants rather tightly (most languages don't; English does to a similar degree but Japanese hardly has any
1863     * groups of consonants), and there are many more vowel sounds without using tones (here, two or three letters are
1864     * used for a vowel, where the first can be y or w and the rest can be a, e, i, o, or u in some combination). Some
1865     * letter combinations possible here are impossible or very rare in correctly-Romanized actual Korean, such as the
1866     * rare occurrence of a single 'l' before a vowel (it normally only appears in Romanized text before a consonant or
1867     * at the end of a word).
1868     * <br>
1869     * Hyeop euryam, sonyon muk tyeok aengyankeon, koelgwaelmwak.
1870     */
1871    public static final FakeLanguageGen KOREAN_ROMANIZED = korean().register();

2088    /**
2089     * Fantasy/sci-fi language that could be spoken by some very-non-human culture that would typically be fitting for
2090     * an alien species. This alien language is meant to have an abrupt change mid-word for many words, with the suffix
2091     * of roughly half of words using the letter "e", which is absent from the rest of the language; these suffixes can
2092     * also use consonant clusters, which are similarly absent elsewhere. The suffixes would make sense as a historical
2093     * relic or as a linguistic holdout from a historical merger. As the name would suggest, it strongly prefers
2094     * using the vowel "u", with it present in about half the groups, and can use the umlaut accent "ü" on some vowels.
2095     * The consonants completely avoid hard sounds like "t" and "k", and don't cluster; they often have special marks.
2096     * This should be relatively easy to pronounce for an alien language, though the words are rather long.
2097     * <br>
2098     * Üweħid vuŕeħid deẃul leŋul waloyeyür; äyovavü...
2099     */
2100    public static final FakeLanguageGen ALIEN_U = alien_u().register();

2180    /**
2181     * Fantasy language that tries to sound like the speech of a powerful and pompous dragon, using long, complex words
2182     * and a mix of hard consonants like "t" and "k", "liquid" consonants like "l" and "r", and sometimes vowel groups
2183     * like "ie" and "aa". It frequently uses consonant clusters involving "r". It uses no accented characters.
2184     * <br>
2185     * Vokegodzaaz kigrofreth ariatarkioth etrokagik deantoznik hragriemitaaz gianehaadaz...
2186     */
2187    public static final FakeLanguageGen DRAGON = dragon().register();
2188
2189    /**
2190     * Fantasy language based closely on {@link #DRAGON}, but with much shorter words normally and closing syllables
2191     * that may sound "rushed" or "crude", though it has the same general frequency of most consonants and vowels.
2192     * This means it still uses lots of "t", "k", and "r", can group two vowels sometimes, and when there's a consonant
2193     * in the middle of a word, it is often accompanied by an "r" on one or both sides. If used with
2194     * {@link NaturalLanguageCipher}, this will look very similar to DRAGON, because the syllable lengths aren't
2195     * determined by this object but by the text being ciphered. Still, the ends of words are often different. It is
2196     * called KOBOLD because, even though the original kobold myth was that of a goblin-like spirit that haunted cobalt
2197     * mines, the modern RPG treatment of kobolds frequently describes them as worshippers of dragons or in some way
2198     * created by dragons, but generally they're a sort of failure to live up to a dragon's high expectations. The feel
2199     * of this language is meant to be something like a dragon's speech, but much less "fancy" and rather curt.
2200     * <br>
2201     * Thritriz, laazak gruz kokak thon lut...
2202     */
2203    public static final FakeLanguageGen KOBOLD = new FakeLanguageGen(
2204            DRAGON.openingVowels, DRAGON.midVowels, DRAGON.openingConsonants, DRAGON.midConsonants, DRAGON.closingConsonants,
2205            new String[]{"ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "et", "ut", "ark", "irk", "erk"},
2206            DRAGON.vowelSplitters, new int[]{1, 2, 3}, new double[]{5, 11, 1},
2207            0.1, 0.0, 0.0, 0.22, genericSanityChecks, true);
2208
2209    /**
2210     * An array that stores all the hand-made FakeLanguageGen constants; it does not store randomly-generated languages
2211     * nor does it store modifications or mixes of languages. The order these are stored in is related to the numeric
2212     * codes for languages in the {@link #serializeToString()} output, but neither is dependent on the other if this
2213     * array is changed for some reason (which is not recommended, but not out of the question). If this is modified,
2214     * then it is probably a bad idea to assign null to any elements in registered; special care is taken to avoid null
2215     * elements in its original state, so some code may rely on the items being usable and non-null.
2216     */
2217    public static final FakeLanguageGen[] registered;
2218
2219    static {
2220        // the first item in registry is null so it can be a placeholder for random languages; we want to skip it.
2221        registered = new FakeLanguageGen[registry.size()-1];
2222        for (int i = 0; i < registered.length; i++) {
2223            registered[i] = registry.getAt(i+1);
2224        }
2225    }

2273    /**
2274     * This is a very complicated constructor! Maybe look at the calls to this to initialize static members of this
2275     * class, LOVECRAFT and GREEK_ROMANIZED.
2276     *
2277     * @param openingVowels        String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear at the start
2278     *                             of a word or in the middle; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2279     * @param midVowels            String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear in the
2280     *                             middle of the word; all openingVowels are automatically copied into this internally.
2281     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2282     * @param openingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster that can appear
2283     *                             at the start of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2284     * @param midConsonants        String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2285     *                             between vowels; all closingConsonants are automatically copied into this internally.
2286     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2287     * @param closingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2288     *                             at the end of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2289     * @param closingSyllables     String array where each element is a syllable starting with a vowel and ending in
2290     *                             whatever the word should end in; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2291     * @param vowelSplitters       String array where each element is a mark that goes between vowels, so if "-" is in this,
2292     *                             then "a-a" may be possible; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2293     * @param syllableLengths      int array where each element is a possible number of syllables a word can use; closely
2294     *                             tied to syllableFrequencies
2295     * @param syllableFrequencies  double array where each element corresponds to an element in syllableLengths and
2296     *                             represents how often each syllable count should appear relative to other counts; there
2297     *                             is no need to restrict the numbers to add up to any other number
2298     * @param vowelStartFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words start with vowels;
2299     *                             higher numbers yield more words starting with vowels
2300     * @param vowelEndFrequency    a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words end with vowels; higher
2301     *                             numbers yield more words ending in vowels
2302     * @param vowelSplitFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that, if vowelSplitters is not empty, determines how
2303     *                             often a vowel will be split into two vowels separated by one of those splitters
2304     * @param syllableEndFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often an element of
2305     *                             closingSyllables is used instead of ending normally
2306     */
2307    public FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2308                           String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables, String[] vowelSplitters,
2309                           int[] syllableLengths, double[] syllableFrequencies, double vowelStartFrequency,
2310                           double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency, double syllableEndFrequency) {
2311        this(openingVowels, midVowels, openingConsonants, midConsonants, closingConsonants, closingSyllables,
2312                vowelSplitters, syllableLengths, syllableFrequencies, vowelStartFrequency, vowelEndFrequency,
2313                vowelSplitFrequency, syllableEndFrequency, englishSanityChecks, true);
2314    }

2316    /**
2317     * This is a very complicated constructor! Maybe look at the calls to this to initialize static members of this
2318     * class, LOVECRAFT and GREEK_ROMANIZED.
2319     *
2320     * @param openingVowels        String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear at the start
2321     *                             of a word or in the middle; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2322     * @param midVowels            String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear in the
2323     *                             middle of the word; all openingVowels are automatically copied into this internally.
2324     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2325     * @param openingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster that can appear
2326     *                             at the start of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2327     * @param midConsonants        String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2328     *                             between vowels; all closingConsonants are automatically copied into this internally.
2329     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2330     * @param closingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2331     *                             at the end of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2332     * @param closingSyllables     String array where each element is a syllable starting with a vowel and ending in
2333     *                             whatever the word should end in; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2334     * @param vowelSplitters       String array where each element is a mark that goes between vowels, so if "-" is in this,
2335     *                             then "a-a" may be possible; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2336     * @param syllableLengths      int array where each element is a possible number of syllables a word can use; closely
2337     *                             tied to syllableFrequencies
2338     * @param syllableFrequencies  double array where each element corresponds to an element in syllableLengths and
2339     *                             represents how often each syllable count should appear relative to other counts; there
2340     *                             is no need to restrict the numbers to add up to any other number
2341     * @param vowelStartFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words start with vowels;
2342     *                             higher numbers yield more words starting with vowels
2343     * @param vowelEndFrequency    a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words end with vowels; higher
2344     *                             numbers yield more words ending in vowels
2345     * @param vowelSplitFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that, if vowelSplitters is not empty, determines how
2346     *                             often a vowel will be split into two vowels separated by one of those splitters
2347     * @param syllableEndFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often an element of
2348     *                             closingSyllables is used instead of ending normally
2349     * @param sane                 true to perform sanity checks for pronounce-able sounds to most English speakers, replacing many
2350     *                             words that are impossible to say; slows down generation slightly, irrelevant for non-Latin alphabets
2351     * @param clean                true to perform vulgarity/obscenity checks on the word, replacing it if it is too close to a
2352     *                             common English vulgarity, obscenity, or slur/epithet; slows down generation slightly
2353     */
2354    public FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2355                           String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables, String[] vowelSplitters,
2356                           int[] syllableLengths, double[] syllableFrequencies, double vowelStartFrequency,
2357                           double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency, double syllableEndFrequency,
2358                           Pattern[] sane, boolean clean) {
2359        this.openingVowels = openingVowels;
2360        this.midVowels = new String[openingVowels.length + midVowels.length];
2361        System.arraycopy(midVowels, 0, this.midVowels, 0, midVowels.length);
2362        System.arraycopy(openingVowels, 0, this.midVowels, midVowels.length, openingVowels.length);
2363        this.openingConsonants = openingConsonants;
2364        this.midConsonants = new String[midConsonants.length + closingConsonants.length];
2365        System.arraycopy(midConsonants, 0, this.midConsonants, 0, midConsonants.length);
2366        System.arraycopy(closingConsonants, 0, this.midConsonants, midConsonants.length, closingConsonants.length);
2367        this.closingConsonants = closingConsonants;
2368        this.vowelSplitters = vowelSplitters;
2369        this.closingSyllables = closingSyllables;
2370
2371        this.syllableFrequencies = new IntDoubleOrderedMap(syllableLengths, syllableFrequencies, 0.75f);
2372
2373        totalSyllableFrequency = this.syllableFrequencies.values().sum();
2374        if (vowelStartFrequency > 1.0)
2375            this.vowelStartFrequency = 1.0 / vowelStartFrequency;
2376        else
2377            this.vowelStartFrequency = vowelStartFrequency;
2378        if (vowelEndFrequency > 1.0)
2379            this.vowelEndFrequency = 1.0 / vowelEndFrequency;
2380        else
2381            this.vowelEndFrequency = vowelEndFrequency;
2382        if (vowelSplitters.length == 0)
2383            this.vowelSplitFrequency = 0.0;
2384        else if (vowelSplitFrequency > 1.0)
2385            this.vowelSplitFrequency = 1.0 / vowelSplitFrequency;
2386        else
2387            this.vowelSplitFrequency = vowelSplitFrequency;
2388        if (closingSyllables.length == 0)
2389            this.syllableEndFrequency = 0.0;
2390        else if (syllableEndFrequency > 1.0)
2391            this.syllableEndFrequency = 1.0 / syllableEndFrequency;
2392        else
2393            this.syllableEndFrequency = syllableEndFrequency;
2394        this.clean = clean;
2395        sanityChecks = sane;
2396        modifiers = new ArrayList<>(16);
2397    }
2398
2399    private FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2400                            String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables,
2401                            String[] vowelSplitters, IntDoubleOrderedMap syllableFrequencies,
2402                            double vowelStartFrequency, double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency,
2403                            double syllableEndFrequency, Pattern[] sanityChecks, boolean clean,
2404                            List<Modifier> modifiers) {
2405        this.openingVowels = copyStrings(openingVowels);
2406        this.midVowels = copyStrings(midVowels);
2407        this.openingConsonants = copyStrings(openingConsonants);
2408        this.midConsonants = copyStrings(midConsonants);
2409        this.closingConsonants = copyStrings(closingConsonants);
2410        this.closingSyllables = copyStrings(closingSyllables);
2411        this.vowelSplitters = copyStrings(vowelSplitters);
2412        this.syllableFrequencies = new IntDoubleOrderedMap(syllableFrequencies);
2413        this.vowelStartFrequency = vowelStartFrequency;
2414        this.vowelEndFrequency = vowelEndFrequency;
2415        this.vowelSplitFrequency = vowelSplitFrequency;
2416        this.syllableEndFrequency = syllableEndFrequency;
2417        for (Double freq : this.syllableFrequencies.values()) {
2418            totalSyllableFrequency += freq;
2419        }
2420        if (sanityChecks == null)
2421            this.sanityChecks = null;
2422        else {
2423            this.sanityChecks = new Pattern[sanityChecks.length];
2424            System.arraycopy(sanityChecks, 0, this.sanityChecks, 0, sanityChecks.length);
2425        }
2426        this.clean = clean;
2427        this.modifiers = new ArrayList<>(modifiers);
2428    }

2430    private static String[] processParts(OrderedMap<String, String> parts, Set<String> missingSounds,
2431                                         Set<String> forbidden, RNG rng, double repeatSingleChance,
2432                                         int preferredLimit) {
2433        int l, sz = parts.size();
2434        List<String> working = new ArrayList<>(sz * 24);
2435        String pair;
2436        for (int e = 0; e < parts.size(); e++) {
2437            Map.Entry<String, String> sn = parts.entryAt(e);
2438            if (missingSounds.contains(sn.getKey()))
2439                continue;
2440            for (String t : sn.getValue().split(" ")) {
2441                if (forbidden.contains(t))
2442                    continue;
2443                l = t.length();
2444                int num;
2445                char c;
2446                switch (l) {
2447                    case 0:
2448                        break;
2449                    case 1:
2450                        working.add(t);
2451                        working.add(t);
2452                        working.add(t);
2453                        c = t.charAt(0);
2454                        num = 0;
2455                        boolean repeat = true;
2456                        switch (c) {
2457                            case 'w':
2458                                num += 2;
2459                            case 'y':
2460                            case 'h':
2461                                num += 4;
2462                            case 'q':
2463                            case 'x':
2464                                num += 4;
2465                                repeat = false;
2466                                break;
2467                            case 'i':
2468                            case 'u':
2469                                repeat = false;
2470                                num = 13;
2471                                break;
2472                            case 'z':
2473                            case 'v':
2474                                num = 4;
2475                                break;
2476                            case 'j':
2477                                num = 7;
2478                                break;
2479                            default:
2480                                if (e >= preferredLimit)
2481                                    num = 6;
2482                                else
2483                                    num = 13;
2484                        }
2485                        for (int i = 0; i < num * 3; i++) {
2486                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.75) {
2487                                working.add(t);
2488                            }
2489                        }
2490
2491                        if (repeat && rng.nextDouble() < repeatSingleChance) {
2492                            pair = t + t;
2493                            if (missingSounds.contains(pair))
2494                                continue;
2495                            working.add(pair);
2496                            working.add(pair);
2497                            working.add(pair);
2498                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.7) {
2499                                working.add(pair);
2500                                working.add(pair);
2501                            }
2502                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.7) {
2503                                working.add(pair);
2504                            }
2505                        }
2506
2507                        break;
2508                    case 2:
2509                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.65) {
2510                            c = t.charAt(1);
2511                            num = 0;
2512                            switch (c) {
2513                                case 'z':
2514                                    num = 1;
2515                                    break;
2516                                case 'w':
2517                                    num = 3;
2518                                    break;
2519                                case 'n':
2520                                    num = 4;
2521                                    break;
2522                                default:
2523
2524                                    if (e >= preferredLimit)
2525                                        num = 2;
2526                                    else
2527                                        num = 7;
2528                            }
2529                            working.add(t);
2530                            for (int i = 0; i < num; i++) {
2531                                if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.25) {
2532                                    working.add(t);
2533                                }
2534                            }
2535                        }
2536                        break;
2537                    case 3:
2538                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.5) {
2539                            c = t.charAt(0);
2540                            switch (c) {
2541                                case 'z':
2542                                    num = 1;
2543                                    break;
2544                                case 'w':
2545                                    num = 3;
2546                                    break;
2547                                case 'n':
2548                                    num = 4;
2549                                    break;
2550                                default:
2551                                    if (e >= preferredLimit)
2552                                        num = 2;
2553                                    else
2554                                        num = 6;
2555                            }
2556                            working.add(t);
2557                            for (int i = 0; i < num; i++) {
2558                                if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.2) {
2559                                    working.add(t);
2560                                }
2561                            }
2562                        }
2563                        break;
2564                    default:
2565                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.3 && (t.charAt(l - 1) != 'z' || rng.nextDouble() < 0.1)) {
2566                            working.add(t);
2567                        }
2568                        break;
2569                }
2570            }
2571        }
2572        return working.toArray(new String[0]);
2573    }

2584    public static FakeLanguageGen randomLanguage(RNG rng) {

2588    public static FakeLanguageGen randomLanguage(long seed) {
2589        StatefulRNG rng = new StatefulRNG(seed);
2590        int[] lengths = new int[rng.between(3, 5)];
2591        System.arraycopy(new int[]{1, 2, 3, 4}, 0, lengths, 0, lengths.length);
2592        double[] chances = new double[lengths.length];
2593        System.arraycopy(new double[]{
2594                5 + rng.nextDouble(4), 13 + rng.nextDouble(9), 3 + rng.nextDouble(3), 1 + rng.nextDouble(2)
2595        }, 0, chances, 0, chances.length);
2596        double vowelHeavy = rng.between(0.2, 0.5), removalRate = rng.between(0.15, 0.65);
2597        int sz = openCons.size();
2598        int[] reordering = rng.randomOrdering(sz), vOrd = rng.randomOrdering(openVowels.size());
2599        OrderedMap<String, String>
2600                parts0 = new OrderedMap<>(openVowels),
2601                parts1 = new OrderedMap<>(openCons),
2602                parts2 = new OrderedMap<>(midCons),
2603                parts3 = new OrderedMap<>(closeCons);
2604        OrderedSet<String> forbidden = new OrderedSet<>(1024, 0.25f), missingSounds = new OrderedSet<>(64, 0.875f);
2605        parts1.reorder(reordering);
2606        parts2.reorder(reordering);
2607        parts3.reorder(reordering);
2608        parts0.reorder(vOrd);
2609        int n = 0;
2610
2611        int mn = Math.min(rng.nextInt(3), rng.nextInt(3)), sz0, p0s;
2612
2613        for (n = 0; n < mn; n++) {
2614            missingSounds.add(parts0.keyAt(0));
2615            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts0.getAt(0).split(" "));
2616            parts0.removeFirst();
2617        }
2618        p0s = parts0.size();
2619        sz0 = Math.max(rng.between(1, p0s + 1), rng.between(1, p0s + 1));
2620        char[] nextAccents = new char[sz0], unaccented = new char[sz0];
2621        int vowelAccent = rng.between(1, 7);
2622        for (int i = 0; i < sz0; i++) {
2623            nextAccents[i] = accentedVowels[vOrd[i + mn]][vowelAccent];
2624            unaccented[i] = accentedVowels[vOrd[i + mn]][0];
2625        }
2626        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.8) {
2627            for (int i = 0; i < sz0; i++) {
2628                char ac = nextAccents[i], ua = unaccented[i];
2629                String v = "", uas = String.valueOf(ua);
2630                Pattern pat = Pattern.compile("\\b([aeiou]*)(" + ua + ")([aeiou]*)\\b");
2631                Replacer rep = pat.replacer("$1$2$3 $1" + ac + "$3"), repLess = pat.replacer("$1" + ac + "$3");
2632                for (int j = 0; j < p0s; j++) {
2633                    String k = parts0.keyAt(j);
2634                    if (uas.equals(k))
2635                        v = parts0.getAt(j);
2636                    else {
2637                        String current = parts0.getAt(j);
2638                        String[] splits = current.split(" ");
2639                        for (int s = 0; s < splits.length; s++) {
2640                            if (forbidden.contains(uas) && splits[s].contains(uas))
2641                                forbidden.add(splits[s].replace(ua, ac));
2642                        }
2643                        parts0.put(k, rep.replace(current));
2644                    }
2645                }
2646                parts0.put(String.valueOf(ac), repLess.replace(v));
2647            }
2648        }
2649
2650        n = 0;
2651        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.75) {
2652            missingSounds.add("z");
2653            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("z").split(" "));
2654            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("z").split(" "));
2655            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("z").split(" "));
2656            n++;
2657        }
2658        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.82) {
2659            missingSounds.add("x");
2660            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("x").split(" "));
2661            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("x").split(" "));
2662            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("x").split(" "));
2663            n++;
2664        }
2665        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.92) {
2666            missingSounds.add("qu");
2667            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("qu").split(" "));
2668            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("qu").split(" "));
2669            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("qu").split(" "));
2670            n++;
2671        }
2672        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.96) {
2673            missingSounds.add("q");
2674            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("q").split(" "));
2675            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("q").split(" "));
2676            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("q").split(" "));
2677            n++;
2678        }
2679        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.97) {
2680            missingSounds.add("tl");
2681            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("tl").split(" "));
2682            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("tl").split(" "));
2683            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("tl").split(" "));
2684            n++;
2685        }
2686        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.86) {
2687            missingSounds.add("ph");
2688            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("ph").split(" "));
2689            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("ph").split(" "));
2690            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("ph").split(" "));
2691            n++;
2692        }
2693        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.94) {
2694            missingSounds.add("kh");
2695            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("kh").split(" "));
2696            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("kh").split(" "));
2697            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("kh").split(" "));
2698            n++;
2699        }
2700        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.96) {
2701            missingSounds.add("bh");
2702            missingSounds.add("dh");
2703            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("bh").split(" "));
2704            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("bh").split(" "));
2705            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("bh").split(" "));
2706            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("dh").split(" "));
2707            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("dh").split(" "));
2708            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("dh").split(" "));
2709            n++;
2710            n++;
2711        }
2712
2713        for (; n < sz * removalRate; n++) {
2714            missingSounds.add(parts1.keyAt(n));
2715            missingSounds.add(parts2.keyAt(n));
2716            missingSounds.add(parts3.keyAt(n));
2717            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.getAt(n).split(" "));
2718            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.getAt(n).split(" "));
2719            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.getAt(n).split(" "));
2720        }
2721
2722        return new FakeLanguageGen(
2723                processParts(parts0, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, 0.0, p0s),
2724                new String[]{},
2725                processParts(openCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, 0.0, 4096),
2726                processParts(midCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, (rng.nextDouble() * 3 - 0.75) * 0.4444, 4096),
2727                processParts(closeCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, (rng.nextDouble() * 3 - 0.75) * 0.2857, 4096),
2728                new String[]{},
2729                new String[]{}, lengths, chances, vowelHeavy, vowelHeavy * 1.8, 0.0, 0.0, genericSanityChecks, true).summarize("0#" + seed + "@1");
2730    }
2731
2732    protected static boolean checkAll(CharSequence testing, Pattern[] checks) {
2733        CharSequence fixed = removeAccents(testing);
2734        for (int i = 0; i < checks.length; i++) {
2735            if (checks[i].matcher(fixed).find())
2736                return false;
2737        }
2738        return true;
2739    }
2740
2741    /**
2742     * Checks a CharSequence, such as a String, against an overzealous vulgarity filter, returning true if the text
2743     * could contain vulgar elements or words that could seem vulgar or juvenile. The idea here is that false positives
2744     * are OK as long as there are very few false negatives (missed vulgar words). Does not check punctuation or numbers
2745     * that could look like letters.
2746     * @param testing the text, as a CharSequence such as a String, to check
2747     * @return true if the text could contain a vulgar or juvenile element; false if it probably doesn't
2748     */
2749    public static boolean checkVulgarity(CharSequence testing)
2750    {
2751        CharSequence fixed = removeAccents(testing);
2752        for (int i = 0; i < vulgarChecks.length; i++) {
2753            if (vulgarChecks[i].matcher(fixed).find())
2754            {
2755                System.out.println(vulgarChecks[i]);
2756                return true;
2757            }
2758        }
2759        return false;
2760    }
2761
2762    /**
2763     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen, using and changing the current seed.
2764     *
2765     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
2766     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
2767     */
2768    public String word(boolean capitalize) {
2769        return word(srng, capitalize);
2770    }
2771
2772    /**
2773     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG.
2774     *
2775     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
2776     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
2777     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
2778     */
2779    public String word(RNG rng, boolean capitalize) {
2780        while (true) {
2781            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
2782            double syllableChance = rng.nextDouble(totalSyllableFrequency);
2783            int syllables = 1, i = 0;
2784            for (IntDoubleOrderedMap.MapEntry kv : syllableFrequencies.mapEntrySet()) {
2785                if (syllableChance < kv.getDoubleValue()) {
2786                    syllables = kv.getIntKey();
2787                    break;
2788                } else
2789                    syllableChance -= kv.getDoubleValue();
2790            }
2791            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
2792                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
2793                if (syllables == 1)
2794                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
2795                else
2796                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
2797                i++;
2798            } else {
2799                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
2800            }
2801            String close = "";
2802            boolean redouble = false;
2803            if (i < syllables) {
2804                if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
2805                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
2806                    if (close.contains("@") && (syllables & 1) == 0) {
2807                        redouble = true;
2808                        syllables = (syllables | 1) >> 1;
2809
2810                        //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
2811                    }
2812                    if (!close.contains("@"))
2813                        ender.append(close);
2814                    else if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
2815                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2816                        if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2817                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2818                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2819                        }
2820                    }
2821                } else {
2822                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2823                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2824                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2825                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2826                    }
2827                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
2828                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
2829                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
2830                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
2831                            if (close.contains("@") && (syllables & 1) == 0) {
2832                                redouble = true;
2833                                syllables = (syllables | 1) >> 1;
2834
2835                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
2836                            }
2837                            if (!close.contains("@"))
2838                                ender.append(close);
2839                        }
2840                    }
2841                }
2842                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
2843
2844            }
2845
2846            for (; i < syllables; i++) {
2847                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2848                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2849                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2850                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2851                }
2852                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
2853            }
2854
2855            sb.append(ender);
2856            if (redouble && i <= syllables + 1) {
2857                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
2858            }
2859
2860            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
2861                continue;
2862
2863            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
2864                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
2865            }
2866
2867            if (capitalize)
2868                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
2869
2870            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
2871                continue;
2872            return sb.toString();
2873        }
2874    }
2875
2876    /**
2877     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG.
2878     *
2879     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
2880     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
2881     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
2882     */
2883    public String word(RNG rng, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables) {
2884        return word(rng, capitalize, approxSyllables, null);
2885    }
2886
2887    /**
2888     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG.
2889     *
2890     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
2891     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
2892     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
2893     */
2894    public String word(RNG rng, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables, Pattern[] additionalChecks) {
2895        if (approxSyllables <= 0) {
2896            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
2897            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
2898                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
2899            }
2900            if (capitalize) sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
2901            return sb.toString();
2902        }
2903        while (true) {
2904            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
2905            int i = 0;
2906            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
2907                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
2908                if (approxSyllables == 1 && closingConsonants.length > 0)
2909                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
2910                else if (midConsonants.length > 0)
2911                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
2912                i++;
2913            } else if (openingConsonants.length > 0) {
2914                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
2915            }
2916            String close = "";
2917            boolean redouble = false;
2918            if (i < approxSyllables) {
2919                if (closingSyllables.length > 0 && rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
2920                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
2921                    if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
2922                        redouble = true;
2923                        approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
2924
2925                        //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
2926                    }
2927                    if (!close.contains("@"))
2928                        ender.append(close);
2929                    else if (redouble && rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
2930                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2931                        if (vowelSplitters.length > 0 && rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2932                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2933                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2934                        }
2935                    }
2936                } else {
2937                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2938                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2939                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2940                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2941                    }
2942                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
2943                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
2944                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
2945                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
2946                            if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
2947                                redouble = true;
2948                                approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
2949
2950                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
2951                            }
2952                            if (!close.contains("@"))
2953                                ender.append(close);
2954                        }
2955                    }
2956                }
2957                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
2958            }
2959
2960            for (; i < approxSyllables; i++) {
2961                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2962                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
2963                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
2964                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
2965                }
2966                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
2967            }
2968
2969            sb.append(ender);
2970            if (redouble && i <= approxSyllables + 1) {
2971                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
2972            }
2973
2974            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
2975                continue;
2976
2977            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
2978                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
2979            }
2980
2981            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
2982                continue;
2983
2984            if (additionalChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, additionalChecks))
2985                continue;
2986
2987            if (capitalize)
2988                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
2989
2990            return sb.toString();
2991        }
2992    }
2993
2994    /**
2995     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG.
2996     *
2997     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
2998     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
2999     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
3000     */
3001    public String word(StatefulRNG rng, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables, long... reseeds) {
3002        if (approxSyllables <= 0) {
3003            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3004            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3005                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3006            }
3007            if (capitalize) sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3008            return sb.toString();
3009        }
3010        int numSeeds, fraction = 1;
3011        if (reseeds != null)
3012            numSeeds = Math.min(reseeds.length, approxSyllables - 1);
3013        else numSeeds = 0;
3014        while (true) {
3015            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
3016            int i = 0;
3017            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
3018                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3019                if (approxSyllables == 1)
3020                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3021                else
3022                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3023                i++;
3024            } else {
3025                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
3026            }
3027            String close = "";
3028            boolean redouble = false;
3029            if (i < approxSyllables) {
3030                if (numSeeds > 0 && i > 0 && i == approxSyllables * fraction / (1 + numSeeds))
3031                    rng.setState(reseeds[fraction++ - 1]);
3032                if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3033                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3034                    if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3035                        redouble = true;
3036                        approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3037                    }
3038                    if (!close.contains("@"))
3039                        ender.append(close);
3040                    else if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
3041                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3042                        if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3043                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
3044                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3045                        }
3046                    }
3047                } else {
3048                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3049                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3050                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
3051                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3052                    }
3053                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
3054                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3055                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3056                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3057                            if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3058                                redouble = true;
3059                                approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3060
3061                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3062                            }
3063                            if (!close.contains("@"))
3064                                ender.append(close);
3065                        }
3066                    }
3067                }
3068                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
3069            }
3070
3071            for (; i < approxSyllables; i++) {
3072                if (numSeeds > 0 && i > 0 && i == approxSyllables * fraction / (1 + numSeeds))
3073                    rng.setState(reseeds[fraction++ - 1]);
3074                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3075                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3076                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters));
3077                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3078                }
3079                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3080            }
3081
3082            sb.append(ender);
3083            if (redouble && i <= approxSyllables + 1) {
3084                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
3085            }
3086
3087            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
3088                continue;
3089
3090            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3091                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3092            }
3093
3094            if (capitalize)
3095                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3096
3097            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
3098                continue;
3099            return sb.toString();
3100        }
3101    }

3112                new String[]{".", ".", ".", "!", "?", "..."}, 0.2);

3134     * @param endPunctuation          a String array where each element is a period, question mark, or the like that goes at

3145    /**
3146     * Generate a sentence from this FakeLanguageGen using the specific RNG.
3147     *
3148     * @param rng                     the RNG to use for the randomized string building
3149     * @param minWords                an int for the minimum number of words in a sentence; should be at least 1
3150     * @param maxWords                an int for the maximum number of words in a sentence; should be at least equal to minWords
3151     * @param midPunctuation          a String array where each element is a comma, semicolon, or the like that goes before a
3152     *                                space in the middle of a sentence
3153     * @param endPunctuation          a String array where each element is a period, question mark, or the like that goes at
3154     *                                the very end of a sentence
3155     * @param midPunctuationFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often Strings from
3156     *                                midPunctuation should be inserted before spaces
3157     * @return a sentence in the gibberish language as a String
3158     */
3159    public String sentence(RNG rng, int minWords, int maxWords, String[] midPunctuation, String[] endPunctuation,
3160                           double midPunctuationFrequency) {
3161        if (minWords < 1)
3162            minWords = 1;
3163        if (minWords > maxWords)
3164            maxWords = minWords;
3165        if (midPunctuationFrequency > 1.0) {
3166            midPunctuationFrequency = 1.0 / midPunctuationFrequency;
3167        }
3168        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(12 * maxWords);
3169        sb.append(word(rng, true));
3170        for (int i = 1; i < minWords; i++) {
3171            if (rng.nextDouble() < midPunctuationFrequency) {
3172                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midPunctuation));
3173            }
3174            sb.append(' ');
3175            sb.append(word(rng, false));
3176        }
3177        for (int i = minWords; i < maxWords && rng.nextInt(2 * maxWords) > i; i++) {
3178            if (rng.nextDouble() < midPunctuationFrequency) {
3179                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midPunctuation));
3180            }
3181            sb.append(' ');
3182            sb.append(word(rng, false));
3183        }
3184        if (endPunctuation != null && endPunctuation.length > 0)
3185            sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(endPunctuation));
3186        return sb.toString();
3187    }

3189    /**
3190     * Generate a sentence from this FakeLanguageGen that fits in the given length limit..
3191     *
3192     * @param minWords                an int for the minimum number of words in a sentence; should be at least 1
3193     * @param maxWords                an int for the maximum number of words in a sentence; should be at least equal to minWords
3194     * @param midPunctuation          a String array where each element is a comma, semicolon, or the like that goes before a
3195     *                                space in the middle of a sentence
3196     * @param endPunctuation          a String array where each element is a period, question mark, or the like that goes at
3197     *                                the very end of a sentence
3198     * @param midPunctuationFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often Strings from
3199     *                                midPunctuation should be inserted before spaces
3200     * @param maxChars                the longest string length this can produce; should be at least {@code 6 * minWords}
3201     * @return a sentence in the gibberish language as a String
3202     */
3203    public String sentence(int minWords, int maxWords, String[] midPunctuation, String[] endPunctuation,
3204                           double midPunctuationFrequency, int maxChars) {
3205        return sentence(srng, minWords, maxWords, midPunctuation, endPunctuation, midPunctuationFrequency, maxChars);
